root.App.Cache.genUrl = function (routeName, context) {
        var route = routeMap[routeName],
            path, keys, i, len, key, param, regex;

        if (!route) { return ''; }

        path = route.path;
        keys = route.keys;

        if (context &amp;&amp; (len = keys.length)) {
            for (i = 0; i &lt; len; i += 1) {
                key   = keys[i];
                param = key.name || key;
                regex = new RegExp('[:*]' + param + '\\b');
                path  = path.replace(regex, context[param]);
            }
        }

        // Replace missing params with empty strings.
        return path.replace(/([:*])([\w\-]+)?/g, '');
    };

src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002Fba024d5cd9f04549fb8321a2172aea4664756a8e.jpg\" width=\"540\" height=\"367\" alt=\"Kids with Severe Allergies Susceptible to &#x2018;Rebound&#x2019; Reactions, Study Finds\"\u003E \n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003E\u003Cb\u003EThese delayed reactions tend to occur when the initial symptoms of an allergic reaction go away, but then return hours or even days later &#x2014; without additional exposure to the \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.livescience.com\u002F36041-common-food-allergies.html\"\u003Esubstance that caused the allergic reaction.\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fb\u003E(Photo: Getty Images)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EIt&#x2019;s fairly common for children who have a severe allergic reaction known as anaphylaxis to be in danger of having a second, delayed allergic reaction within hours of the first one, a new study suggests.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EResearchers in Canada found that about 15 percent of children who came to the emergency room for anaphylaxis had a second \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.livescience.com\u002F48636-this-girl-nearly-died-from-orange-allergy.html\"\u003Eserious allergic reaction hours\u003C\u002Fa\u003E after the initial reaction.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThe study also found that about 75 percent of these second anaphylactic reactions, known as biphasic reactions, occurred within 6 hours of their first anaphylaxis symptoms, and in most cases, the children were still at the ER because of their first reaction. The children&#x2019;s symptoms included difficulty breathing, low blood pressure, hives or swelling, nausea and dizziness.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;The study found that delayed reactions were more likely to happen if the initial allergic reaction in children was severe, and if it was not treated with epinephrine,&#x201D; said Dr. Waleed Alqurashi, the study&#x2019;s lead author and an emergency physician at Children&#x2019;s Hospital of Eastern Ontario in Ottawa, Canada.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated:&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.livescience.com\u002F35479-nine-weirdest-allergies-110215.html\"\u003E8\u003Ci\u003E Strange Signs You&#x2019;re Having an Allergic Reaction\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThese delayed reactions tend to occur when the initial symptoms of an allergic reaction go away, but then return hours or even days later &#x2014; without additional exposure to the \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.livescience.com\u002F36041-common-food-allergies.html\"\u003Esubstance that caused the allergic reaction\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, he said.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EOne possible reason children may develop these delayed allergic reactions is that they seem to experience an inflammatory response that lasts longer than it does in adults, Alqurashi said.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EIn children, common triggers of these serious allergic reactions might include insect stings, medications, and foods like nuts, seafood, milk and eggs, he said.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EAn anaphylactic reaction is a medical emergency requiring immediate treatment with a shot of the hormone epinephrine (adrenaline). Many kids who are at risk of having these serious allergic reactions are advised to carry \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.livescience.com\u002F42321-know-how-to-use-epipen.html\"\u003Ean EpiPen\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, a prescription medication that can be self-administered or given by a parent or school nurse, to control symptoms that can come on rapidly and worsen quickly and, in some cases, be fatal. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EDelayed treatment\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThe occurrence of anaphylactic reactions in children seems to be on the rise, according to the researchers. But there&#x2019;s limited information about how frequently children go on to have a second severe allergic reaction, or about which children might be more vulnerable to having them.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EIn the study, published online June 22 in the journal Annals of Allergy, Asthma and Immunology, the researchers analyzed the medical records of about 500 children who were treated at the emergency rooms of two large Canadian children&#x2019;s hospitals over a one-year period.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThe findings suggested that children who may be at increased risk for delayed allergic reactions are those who were given medications for asthma at the hospital, had signs of anaphylactic shock when they arrived at the emergency room and needed multiple treatments with epinephrine for their initial anaphylactic reaction, Alqurashi said.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EIn addition, the results showed that anaphylaxis tended to be more severe in children when epinephrine administration was delayed.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;Epinephrine is the single \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.livescience.com\u002F41181-obama-signs-epipen-law.html\"\u003Emost important treatment for anaphylaxis\u003C\u002Fa\u003E,&#x201D; Alqurashi said. He explained that, when the drug is given promptly after the start of an allergic reaction, it controls and limits the immune system&#x2019;s response to a known allergy trigger. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;The key message for parents, caregivers and first responders is to administer epinephrine at the first sign of a severe allergic reaction to prevent anaphylaxis from worsening,&#x201D; Alqurashi said.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EAfter that, people should get to the emergency room, he said.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EMore from She did not expect, however, for the machine to throw her to the ground the moment she stepped on.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe treadmill&#x2019;s previous user had not turned the machine off, and the belt was spinning at such a fast clip that it looked motionless. When Myers hit the surface, she tried to get up, but was tossed from the exercise machine instead.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;My nose and face were cut to pieces and my arms were throbbing from burns,&#x201D; the South Manchester, UK mother-of-four told \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.dailymail.co.uk\u002Ffemail\u002Farticle-3158486\u002FMaimed-TREADMILL-Mother-four-s-horror-one-thousands-badly-injured-running-machine.html\"\u003EThe Daily Mail\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. &#x201C;I also had a gash on my forehead. I looked as though I&#x2019;d been in a fight.&quot;Even regular gym-goers like Myers, who was an avid treadmill user, are not immune to the dangers of this piece of exercise equipment.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThis also isn&#x2019;t the first time treadmill accidents have made news in recent months.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ESurveyMonkey CEO Dave Goldberg, husband of Facebook COO Sheryl Sandberg, died this year in a tragic treadmill accident. On May 1, he fell off a machine while on vacation in Mexico, potentially \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.people.com\u002Farticle\u002Fsheryl-sandberg-husband-died-heart-related-causes-dave-goldberg\"\u003Edue to heart complications\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, and sustained a head injury, according to a report in \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.nytimes.com\u002F2015\u002F05\u002F05\u002Ftechnology\u002Fdave-goldberg-cause-of-death.html?smid=nytnow-share&amp;smprod=nytnow&amp;_r=0\"\u003EThe New York Times\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EWe don&#x2019;t often think of danger when we head to the gym, but stepping on a treadmill always poses risks. In 2014, around 24,400 injuries occurred as the direct result of treadmill use &#x2014; almost 40 percent of the 62,600 injuries from exercise equipment, making these machines the most dangerous you&#x2019;ll find in your gym.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003EDeaths\u003C\u002Fi\u003E from treadmill use, on the other hand, are much rarer, according to U.S. Consumer Product Safety Commission data. Only 30 fatalities from treadmills were reported between 2003 and 2012, for an average of just three per yearHere are some checks to make before you start exercising, or while you&#x2019;re in the middle of a workout, from Michael Jonesco, MD, a sports medicine physician at The Ohio State University Wexner Medical Center:&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EEnter with a clean bill of health.\u003C\u002Fb\u003EYour top priority before you hit the gym is to make sure you know your health status. &#x201C;A lot of times we&#x2019;ll see, if you&#x2019;re running, why did he collapse?&#x201D;Jonesco tells Yahoo Health. &#x201C;The most common cause of falling is a vascular event, like a heart attack. I don&#x2019;t know this case, but before you start a workout, always make sure you have a clean bill of health. Continue to be screened for coronary issues, even if you feel healthy &#x2013; especially if you have risk factors like age, being male, or a high-stress job.&#x201D;&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EBeware of strange symptoms.\u003C\u002Fb\u003EIf you&#x2019;re on the treadmill and you feel any chest pain, any shortness of breath beyond what you&#x2019;re used to in a given workout, or any lightheadedness, you need to step off. &#x201C;Lightheadedness is one most people don&#x2019;t think of,&#x201D;says Jonesco. &#x201C;But it can show you&#x2019;re not getting enough blood supply to the brain, and be a preceding factor for passing out.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EDon\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cb\u003E&#x2019;\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cb\u003Et add distractions (until you\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cb\u003E&#x2019;\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cb\u003Ere comfortable).\u003C\u002Fb\u003EBesides coronary issues, other reasons for treadmill falls can usually be pinned to distraction. &#x201C;Usually you have a comfort zone if you&#x2019;re on a machine you&#x2019;re used to, but if you&#x2019;re on vacation or using an unfamiliar machine, you want to take time to get used to it,&#x201D;Jonesco says. Start your workout at a slower pace, be aware of the width of the band, and ditch the headphones or TV until you find your rhythm.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated: \u003Ci\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fhealth\u002F7-treadmill-mistakes-you-might-be-making-91318038937.html?soc_src=mail&amp;soc_trk=ma\"\u003ETreadmill Mistakes You May Be Making\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EUse the safety tabs. \u003C\u002Fb\u003EYou know the attachments on the treadmill, that are meant to immediately stop the machine if you step out of line? They might be annoying, but use &#x2018;em, says Jonesco. &#x201C;A lot of people overlook the safety tabs because they&#x2019;re clunky, but they&#x2019;re there for a reason.&#x201D;Those attachments could prevent a fall, and are especially important if your treadmill is close to the wall in an unfamiliar area. &#x201C;I like to move the machine away from the wall if at all possible,&#x201D;Jonesco says. &#x201C;If you fall and it doesn&#x2019;t turn off, you can get pushed up against the wall, the band will keep moving and can give you some pretty bad abrasions.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EKeep help nearby.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fb\u003EAccording to the report, Goldberg wasn&#x2019;t found by his brother until 7 p.m., although he left for the gym at 4 p.m. Although the gym seems pretty safe, still tell someone you&#x2019;re going &#x2014; or preferably, take them along. &#x201C;Have a workout buddy, or at least familiarize yourself with the people around you at the gym or the staff if something were to happen,&#x201D;says Jonesco. &#x201C;Keep your cell phone nearby you in case of an emergency.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated: \u003Ci\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fhealth\u002F7-ways-to-make-your-treadmill-runs-more-effective-107228499668.html?soc_src=mail&amp;soc_trk=ma\"\u003E7 Ways To Make Your Treadmill Run More Effective&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ENevertheless, exercise is essential. Just, like anything, don&#x2019;t take safety as a given. Always be smart about using equipment, says Jonesco. &#x201C;It&#x2019;s very sad, and could have been a freak thing,&#x201D;he explains. &#x201C;The benefits of exercise far, far exceed the risks.&#x201D;\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003ELet&#x2019;s keep in touch! \n\u003Cp\u003EA \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.reuters.com\u002Farticle\u002F2015\u002F06\u002F17\u002Favvo-inc-survey-idUSnPnc2dhXv+82+PRN20150617\"\u003Enew survey\u003C\u002Fa\u003E of more than 2,000 people conducted by the online legal services marketplace Avvo suggests that people who live on the west coast are more likely to be cheaters.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EAccording to survey results, 20 percent of west coasters say they&#x2019;ve cheated on a partner, compared to 17 percent of southerners, 16 percent of people in the northeast, and 10 percent of they&#x2019;ve had sex with someone who wasn&#x2019;t their partner. (On the flipside, 13 percent of women said they&#x2019;ve cheated.)\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EBut let&#x2019;s go back to the west coast&#x2026;what&#x2019;s that about? Licensed clinical psychologist Ramani Durvasula, Ph.D., says it may be more about where on the west coast most of the survey respondents lived. If people in larger cities participated, then she&#x2019;s not shocked by the findings.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;These cities are filled with transplants,&#x201D; she says. &#x201C;The very personality traits that lead to someone relocating are likely to result in greater openness, and that can also translate into more &#x2018;a-moral&#x2019; behaviors, such as cheating.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated:\u003C\u002Fb\u003E \u003Ci\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.womenshealthmag.com\u002Fsex-and-relationships\u002Fhaving-an-affair?cid=Synd_Yahoo_July15_ShouldYouALWAYSTellYourPartnerifYouCheat\"\u003E\u003Cb\u003EShould You ALWAYS Tell Your Partner if You Cheat?\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EShe points out that L.A. in particular might have a higher-than-normal rate of cheaters since it&#x2019;s a creative city that &#x201C;may be more populated by those higher in the trait of openness, which may be more likely to translate into infidelity.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EOf course, psychiatrist Gail Saltz, M.D., author of \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.amazon.com\u002FAnatomy-Secret-Life-Psychology-Living\u002Fdp\u002F0767922743\"\u003EAnatomy of a Secret Life: The Psychology of Living a Lie\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, points out that infidelity happens everywhere, and people who live on the west coast shouldn&#x2019;t suddenly freak out and assume that their partner will cheat. (And the reverse is true, too&#x2014;Midwesterners shouldn&#x2019;t be super smug about their apparently lack of cheating.)\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EShe says other factors are much more likely to increase the risk that a person will cheat, like whether they&#x2019;ve been raised with infidelity in their family, if they&#x2019;re in a much more liberal environment where a lot of people aren&#x2019;t getting married, and if there is a lot of cheating happening around them. &#x201C;That will change your perception of how okay it is to be unfaithful,&#x201D; she says.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated:\u003C\u002Fb\u003E \u003Ci\u003E\u003Ca Once, Will They Cheat Again?\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EOf course, no cheating is good, and it sucks that anyone reports doing it.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EBut there is a positive side to the study: Nearly 95 percent of the people surveyed say they&#x2019;re happy in their relationship.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E Here, a healthy, low-cal sampling Roti Mediterranean Grill.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fb\u003E(Photo: Instagram \u002F @rotiusa)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EElegant dining has its perks, but sometimes all you want is to get food off of your mind and into your belly, quick&#x2014;and that&#x2019;s when fast-food temptation comes knocking.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe problem is, the faster the food, the less nutritious it tends to be. But that&#x2019;s starting to change. Although burger joints and mall foods still reign (taco) supreme, a new breed of healthy, fast-casual restaurants are sprouting up around the country. In fact, these nutrition-packed options are growing at 10 times the rate of traditional fast-food joints like McDonald&#x2019;s and Wendy&#x2019;s&#x2014;Americans spent more than $21 billion at fast food restaurants like Chipotle in 2014 alone. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EWith smart choices like salmon, guacamole and cold-pressed juices available for grab-and-go, settling for McNuggets because &#x201C;there&#x2019;s nothing else to eat&#x201D; won&#x2019;t cut it anymore. So skip the old-school drive-thrus like McDonald&#x2019;s and Burger King. These seven \u003Ci\u003EEat This, Not That!\u003C\u002Fi\u003E-approved restaurants will whip you up something better&#x2014;and healthier&#x2014;in no time.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"540\" height=\"432\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002Fe8966ea2695deb716324dcfa5c95e7a8e8245735.jpg\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003E(Photo: Courtesy of Dig Inn)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E#1 HEALTHIEST NEW CHAIN\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EDig Inn\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EIt&#x2019;s like: \u003C\u002Fb\u003EA bizarro world Cracker Barrell, where everything is healthy\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EPicture a deluxe Sunday family dinner spread, with all your favorite fixin&#x2019;s&#x2014;minus all the unhealthy casseroles and pies&#x2014;and you&#x2019;ve got Dig Inn. It&#x2019;s a seasonal market-style eatery that offers delicious, locally-sourced and reasonably-priced meals. You can make your own plate by picking a base (salad or whole grain), a protein (lean meat, tofu, or salmon), and then a few sides, and that&#x2019;s when things get interesting. On a recent visit, we saw roasted sweet potatoes, pan-sauteed cauliflower, crunchy summer couscous and kale and rhubarb salad. Reasons Why You Should Have More Sex\" width=\"540\" height=\"270\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ci\u003EIt&#x2019;s a well-known fact that most men don&#x2019;t need more reasons to have sex, but how many guys actually stop to think about the fact that sex could play a key role in their overall health and well-being?\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Ci\u003E (Photo: Getty Images)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ERegular sexual activity is more than recreational; good sexual health is vital to a man&#x2019;s overall physical, psychological and emotional health. Sex can potentially benefit everything from a man&#x2019;s short-term mood, to longer-term issues like cardiovascular health and the reduced risk of prostate cancer.\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EIn addition, sex is a cost-effective and enjoyable way to ensure your long-term health. It&#x2019;s cheaper than a gym membership and a lot better for your waistline than a nightly six pack. With the average man being more mindful than ever about both his budget and his health, sex might be just what the doctor ordered.\u003Cbr\u003E\u003Cbr\u003EHere are 5 reasons sex makes men healthier &#x2013; so get busy tonight.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Ch2\u003E1. Calorie Burn\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E While sex alone may not be enough to create bulging&#xA0;biceps and washboard abs, intercourse definitely gets the blood pumping by raising the heart rate and burning calories. Estimates show that an average session between the sheets can burn 85 to upwards of 200 calories in 30 minutes. If you spent half an hour having sex daily, that could lead to a weight loss of 10 pounds or more over the course of a year. And it&#x2019;s hopefully more fun than a run on the treadmill. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated\u003Ci\u003E:&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.askmen.com\u002Ftop_10\u002Fdating\u002Fbest-sex-positions.html\"\u003E\u003Ci\u003ETop 10 Best Sex Positions\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Ch2\u003E2. Strength Training\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E In addition to burning calories, sex aids in testosterone production, which can strengthen bones and muscles. Testosterone is also responsible for maintaining healthy energy levels, mood, fertility, and sexual desire. So having sex today could help keep your sex drive up down the road. Decreasing testosterone levels, known as andropause or male menopause, can result in a number of side effects including decreased libido, fatigue and depression, among others.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated:\u003Ci\u003E \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.askmen.com\u002Fdating\u002Flove_tip\u002F59_love_tip.html\"\u003E7 Sexual Positions Women Enjoy \u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Ch2\u003E3. Cancer Prevention\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E A number of studies show that men who ejaculate on a regular basis are more than 30% less likely to develop&#xA0;prostate cancer. &#xA0;Regular ejaculation, whether from intercourse or masturbation, help flush out the prostate, which may help curb the development of prostate cancer.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Ch2\u003E4. Improved Cardiovascular Health\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E Because sex is a good form of exercise, it makes sense that it would positively impact the health of your heart. A study from Queens University shows that men who have sex more than three times a week cut their risk of heart attack and stroke in half. Sex has also been shown to lower blood pressure, which further accounts for the overall positive impact on cardiovascular health. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated: \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.askmen.com\u002Ftop_10\u002Fdating\u002Fsex-basics.html\"\u003E\u003Ci\u003E10 Sex Basics To Up Your Bedroom Game\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Ch2\u003E5. Stress Relief\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E The decreased blood pressure that can result from sex could help lower your stress level. Various study participants have been shown to have a smaller rise in blood pressure during stressful situations after sex, as compared to other test subjects. Moreover, sex releases feel-good endorphins that can help lower anxiety. debate\u003C\u002Fa\u003E sprang back into action after Morgan Brian of the U.S. and Alexandra Popp of Germany cracked heads while both attempting to head the ball in a Woman&#x2019;s World Cup semifinal game. Both were visibly injured, but deemed well enough to quickly return to playing in the game by their team doctors &#x2014; and \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.nytimes.com\u002F2015\u002F07\u002F02\u002Fsports\u002Fsoccer\u002Fwomens-world-cup-semifinal-injuries-morgan-brian-alexandra-popp.html\"\u003Ereignited conversation\u003C\u002Fa\u003E that the&#xA0;F&#xE9;d&#xE9;ration Internationale de Football Association (FIFA) is not doing enough to protect its players.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;Intuitively it sounds great,&#x201D; said \u003Ca\u003EDawn Comstock\u003C\u002Fa\u003E of \u003Ca\u003EColorado School of Public Health\u003C\u002Fa\u003E at the \u003Ca\u003EUniversity of Colorado\u003C\u002Fa\u003E Anschutz Medical Campus in Aurora. &#x201C;It even has the word &#x2018;head&#x2019; in it.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EComstock and her colleagues report in JAMA Pediatrics that players are more likely to get concussions during heading than other \u003Ca\u003Esoccer\u003C\u002Fa\u003E plays, but it&#x2019;s not the cause of the\u003Ca\u003Einjuries\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;When you look more deeply in the data, it&#x2019;s not the act of athletes hitting the balls with their heads at all,&#x201D; Comstock said. &#x201C;Rather, it&#x2019;s athlete-to-athlete contact that occurs during heading.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe Safer \u003Ca\u003ESoccer\u003C\u002Fa\u003E campaign, promoted by the nonprofit \u003Ca\u003EBoston\u003C\u002Fa\u003E-based \u003Ca\u003ESports Legacy Institute\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, urges that heading be delayed until high school or age 14. The campaign is backed by professional \u003Ca\u003Esoccer\u003C\u002Fa\u003E players.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ETo see if the data support a ban on heading, the researchers studied a representative sample of U.S. high school \u003Ca\u003Esoccer\u003C\u002Fa\u003E players. Overall, between 2005 and 2014, 627 concussions occurred during 1,393,753 \u003Ca\u003Esoccer\u003C\u002Fa\u003E practices or competitions.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EPlayer-on-player contact was the most common cause of concussions overall, they found.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EHeading was the most common \u003Ca\u003Esoccer\u003C\u002Fa\u003E-related play associated with concussions, compared to other plays like passing or defending the ball. Heading accounted for about 31 percent of concussions among boys and about a quarter of concussions among girls.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EBut about 78 percent and about 62 percent of heading-relate concussions among boys and girls, respectively, were due to contact with another player.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EWhile some young players do get concussions when they head the ball, that number is very small compared to those who are injured by another player while heading the ball, Comstock said.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe current rules of \u003Ca\u003Esoccer\u003C\u002Fa\u003E in many leagues reduce player-to-player contact, she said.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;If we just enforce those kind of rules to eliminate or at least reduce athlete-to-athlete impacts, that would do more to reduce concussions than just banning heading alone,&#x201D; Comstock said.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EDr. \u003Ca\u003ERobert Cantu\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, co-founder and medical director of the \u003Ca\u003ESports Legacy Institute\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, told Reuters Health that the new study confirms previous research on the rate of concussion during heading.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;What (Comstock) does point out - and she&#x2019;s looking at the high school level not the youth level - is that rough play also needs to be addressed,&#x201D; said Cantu, who was not involved with the new study. His organization supports that, he said.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated: \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fhealth\u002Fhow-to-overcome-depression-after-a-sports-injury-92559471297.html\"\u003E\u003Ci\u003EHow to Overcome Depression After a Sports Injury\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EHeading is still the activity with the highest incidence, he pointed out. Also, under age 14 is when the maximum development of the brain occurs.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;By banning headers before (age) 14 we can take 30 percent of concussions down to zero overnight,&#x201D; said Christopher Nowinski, the \u003Ca\u003ESports Legacy Institute\u003C\u002Fa\u003E&#x2019;s co-founder and executive director.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EDr. \u003Ca\u003EJeffrey Bazarian\u003C\u002Fa\u003E of the \u003Ca\u003EUniversity of Rochester\u003C\u002Fa\u003E Medical Center in New York also cautioned that it would be difficult to know how many concussions could be prevented by enforcing current rules.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;When two players go up for a head ball, they&#x2019;re both following the rules,&#x201D; said Bazarian, who wasn&#x2019;t involved with the new research.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EHe stressed that concussions are treatable, and the real question is how repeated hits to players&#x2019; heads impact them later on.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe authors also note out that most \u003Ca\u003Einjuries\u003C\u002Fa\u003E reported in \u003Ca\u003Esoccer\u003C\u002Fa\u003E are to lower parts of the body, not the head.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERead This Next:&#xA0;\u003Ci\u003E\u003Ca Shockingly Harrowing Details of Bunion Surgery","summary":"It began with a bunion on my left foot. Its my mothers fault, I muttered to myself. If she hadnt insisted on my taking those black, slingback shoes that looked like Jimmy Choo knock offs, my foot would not look the way it did.","body":"\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F4244687a62676e00514fb51fcaf634c93b4a54ed.jpg\" width=\"540\" height=\"720\" alt=\"The Shockingly Harrowing Details of Bunion Surgery\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ci\u003EThree weeks on crutches, 8 weeks in special shoes, and only washing your feet once weekly during that time? Who knew? One woman shares her story of bunion surgery.\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Ci\u003E (Photo: Getty Images)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EIt began with a \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fhealth.usnews.com\u002Fhealth-news\u002Fhealth-wellness\u002Farticles\u002F2015\u002F06\u002F01\u002F5-embarrassing-foot-conditions-and-what-you-can-do-about-them\" title=\"Link: null\"\u003Ebunion on my left foot\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;It&#x2019;s my mother&#x2019;s fault,&#x201D; I muttered to myself. If she hadn&#x2019;t insisted on my taking those black, slingback shoes that looked like Jimmy Choo knock offs, my foot would not look the way it did.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EI conveniently forgot I had a choice and didn&#x2019;t have to accept, much less wear the shoes in the first place, regardless of how they accentuated my already shapely calves.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ESlowly, I watched my large left toe migrate toward the second toe, and in the process, the joint in the big toe kept moving outward. When the orb became red and caused pain while walking, I knew it was time to see an orthopedic foot surgeon. Two weeks and two X-rays later, the surgeon explained the procedure, including the recuperation period, which would be three weeks on crutches, keeping the foot dry and a total of eight weeks in a special &#x201C;bunion&#x201D; shoe. I hoped they at least came in multiple color choices.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThere would be six weekly visits after the stitches were removed for routine dressing changes. I had to resist the urge to wrinkle my nose at the thought of not bathing my foot for eight weeks, and the pungent odor that would permeate the air around my healing apendage. The surgeon assured me foot cleansing would be performed by his assistant when the bandages were changed. I felt better knowing proper foot hygiene would occur at least once a week during that time period.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" width=\"540\" height=\"360\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F0ef7c2f70f6e7ad238a22c588980789b9d5f1243.jpg\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003E\u003Cb\u003EAn x-ray of feet with bunions.\u003C\u002Fb\u003E (Photo: Getty Images)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EMy first \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fhealth.usnews.com\u002Fhealth-news\u002Farticles\u002F2015\u002F03\u002F13\u002Frecovery-from-bunion-surgery-faster-than-in-past\"\u003Ebunionectomy\u003C\u002Fa\u003E was performed six weeks later. I woke up in pain, vaguely conscious my left foot felt unnaturally bulky. Miraculously, modern medicine intervened in the form of a narcotic injection, and I fell into a drug-induced sleep. What seemed like only moments later, I was told it was time to dress and go home; \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fhealth.usnews.com\u002Fhealth-news\u002Farticles\u002F2014\u002F08\u002F29\u002Ftake-steps-to-control-bunions\"\u003Ebunion correction\u003C\u002Fa\u003E is a same-day procedure. I barely remember being escorted to my friend&#x2019;s car or the ride home.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ELinda fed me soup and crackers, put me to bed and stayed with me in case I needed assistance getting up during the night. I was grateful she was such a good friend. Burning, throbbing pain woke me the next morning. Medication intended to ease the pain, upset my empty stomach and promptly came back up. Linda blanched visibly, handed me a wastebasket, promptly told me I was on my own and was out the door. Appreciative thoughts exited with her departure. The rest of the day was spent alone, in a pain-induced fog. Fear of another nausea attack stopped me from taking the medication. Who would empty the wastebasket? Phone calls between doctors followed, as I pleaded to go to the hospital for observation. No one seemed to know who had the authority to admit me &#x2013; the surgeon or my primary care physician. Late at night the impasse broke, and permission was granted for admission.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EFrustration with the after hours, snail-like pace of admission procedures provided the perfect opportunity to hone my skill of yelling at the top of my lungs. Linda tried to distract me by doing her imitation of an elk in rutting season, which always induced fits of laughter. It did. Briefly. I promptly resumed voicing my displeasure several octaves higher than before, hoping this behavior would get someone to at least acknowledge my existence and alleviate my pain. I was hoarse from yelling by the time that finally happened.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EI spent two days in the hospital receiving narcotic medication and sleeping \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fhealth.usnews.com\u002Fhealth-news\u002Fpatient-advice\u002Fslideshows\u002F12-questions-to-ask-before-discharge\"\u003Ebefore being discharged\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. Once again, Linda drove me home.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EFor the following two weeks, I reclined on the couch, my foot encased in the boring, black bunion shoe, elevated higher than my heart, watching E-Hollywood, Lifetime and A&amp;E on television. The following week I was back at my desk, and six weeks later, wearing regular shoes.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EA year and a half later, I had a d&#xE9;j&#xE0; vu experience as I looked at my right foot. It was beginning to resemble the left foot prior to surgery. I knew the same fate had befallen my right foot, and another bunionectomy was just a footprint away. &#x201C;I&#x2019;ll bounce back faster if I have surgery now instead of waiting until I&#x2019;m older,&#x201D; I reasoned. Being slightly vain and wanting to have a matched set, I again saw the surgeon for a consultation.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EFour weeks later, a bunionectomy was performed on my right foot. Before the \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fhealth.usnews.com\u002Fhealth-news\u002Fpatient-advice\u002Farticles\u002F2014\u002F07\u002F28\u002Fare-you-getting-the-right-anesthetic\"\u003Eanesthetic\u003C\u002Fa\u003E took effect, I commented on the music in the operating room and requested acoustic guitar be played during surgery. Please, no country\u002Fwestern. I woke up in the recovery room and then again in Pod C, where I spent the next couple hours until the effects of the spinal wore off. A few hours later, I was home, resting on the couch. My recuperation was the same, and the routine didn&#x2019;t bother me the first several days.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EPerhaps because it was spring and the sun beckoned, I was restless. Sitting on the couch gave me ample time to notice the lint on the rugs, dust in the corners and dirt on the linoleum kitchen floor. I had cleaned before the surgery, but dirt and dust have lives of their own and seem to take the commandment\u003Ci\u003Ebe fruitful and multiply\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003Ci\u003E \u003C\u002Fi\u003Eseriously.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EBeing mobility challenged was no excuse to compromise my cleaning standards. I figured out a way to vacuum on crutches. Using the vacuum cleaner as one crutch, and the other crutch under my right arm, I slowly maneuvered the vacuum on the carpet, cleaning small sections at a time, trying hard to avoid bumping into the furniture. I had to stop every few feet to move the crutch that wasn&#x2019;t being used, and position it along the wall. The muscles in my upper torso were getting toned from this workout, as were the muscles in my upper arms from using crutches. &#x201C;I&#x2019;ll be buff in no time,&#x201D; I thought.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ENext came &#x201C;combing&#x201D; the fringe on the area rugs. This required balancing and bending my good leg, holding both crutches on the hand rest with my right arm and leaning forward with the vacuum attachment. When one area of the fringe was &#x201C;coiffed,&#x201D; I hopped to the next section until the fringe was perfectly straight. After my workout, I collapsed on the couch, feeling as if I&#x2019;d just scaled one of the seven peaks, too exhausted to appreciate my accomplishment. When Linda came to visit I admonished her to step over the fringe so as not to disturb its symmetry. She threw me a pathetic look.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ENow, 20-plus years later, and foot surgery trials a dim memory. I love \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fhealth.usnews.com\u002Fhealth-news\u002Farticles\u002F2012\u002F06\u002F14\u002Fpedicure-or-pedicurse-proceed-with-caution\"\u003Eshowing off my feet\u003C\u002Fa\u003E in a pair of slinky, snappy sandals with \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fhealth.usnews.com\u002Fhealth-news\u002Fhealth-wellness\u002Farticles\u002F2013\u002F10\u002F07\u002Ffoot-health-101-learn-how-to-treat-your-feet\" title=\"Link: http:\u002F\u002Fhealth.usnews.com\u002Fhealth-news\u002Fhealth-wellness\u002Farticles\u002F2013\u002F10\u002F07\u002Ffoot-health-101-learn-how-to-treat-your-feet\"\u003Eno unsightly bunions\u003C\u002Fa\u003E to mar their beauty. I&#x2019;ll never again have \u003Ci\u003Ebunion blues\u003C\u002Fi\u003E! I only have \u003Ci\u003Etwo\u003C\u002Fi\u003E feet!\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003E- By Lois Fink&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003ELois Fink is an inspirational speaker, patient advocate and published writer. Work (Yes, Right at Your Desk)\" width=\"540\" height=\"720\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003E\u003Cb\u003EYour chair could really be messing up your posture.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fb\u003E(Photo:&#xA0;Bill&#xA0;\u003Ci\u003EDiodato\u003C\u002Fi\u003E)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ETreadmill desks have been gaining popularity again among women with offices&#x2014;and deep pockets. And while they definitely can help increase your physical activity at the office, a recent study shows that they have one major drawback: decreased productivity. We found eight less distracting items to add to your office (or cubicle) if you&#x2019;re looking to stay active and lose weight this summer.&#xA0;\u003Ci\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E1. Keep a scale under your desk. \u003C\u002Fb\u003EAnd we highly suggest you make it a smart scale. Step on the Withings smart body analyzer, $149.95, when you walk into work, then peruse its collected data&#x2014;your weight and body fat measurements, Body Mass Index, pulse, air quality, weight history, and more&#x2014;as you go through your work-related emails. The scale will use your office&#x2019;s Wi-Fi to send stats directly to your inbox!\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E2. Swap your office chair for a stability ball.\u003C\u002Fb\u003E Balancing on a blown-up ball engages your core and back, but more important, it keeps you moving, says Heather Milton, MS, clinical exercise physiologist at the Center for Musculoskeletal Care at NYU Langone Medical Center. &#x201C;You&#x2019;re shifting more than when you&#x2019;re simply sitting in a chair, which keeps you from being completely sedentary,&#x201D; she explains. Consider splurging on Gaiam&#x2019;s custom fit balance ball chair ($79.98), which gives you the option of placing the ball into a stabilized, ergonomic chair when your abs need relief.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated: \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.glamour.com\u002Fsex-love-life\u002Fblogs\u002Fsmitten\u002F2015\u002F06\u002Fsigns-he-is-in-love-men-boyfriend?mbid=synd_yhealth\"\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ci\u003E25 Unmistakable Signs He&#x2019;s in Love With You\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E2. &#x2026;or lose your chair entirely.\u003C\u002Fb\u003E &#x201C;Stand while you&#x2019;re on a phone call, or initiate a standing meeting,&#x201D; suggests Milton. (Note: \u003Ci\u003EGlamour\u003C\u002Fi\u003E staffers have a stand-up meeting every morning.) Not only will these activities kick your metabolism into high gear, they&#x2019;ll &#x201C;actually increase productivity, because you&#x2019;re increasing your blood flow, which increases your cognitive focus,&#x201D; says Milton.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E3. Use a swivel footrest.\u003C\u002Fb\u003E It&#x2019;s a great idea to prop your feet on a footrest for simple ergonomics. But selecting one such as the Webble ($149.99), which tilts, turns, and slides, keeps your lower body busy and your metabolism high&#x2014;like you would on a treadmill&#x2014;without losing your breath or focus.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E4. Stash sneakers under your desk. \u003C\u002Fb\u003EYou won&#x2019;t be able to pop into that last-minute rowing class when you find yourself leaving work early&#x2014;unless you&#x2019;re prepared. So, &#x201C;decrease all the obstacles that prevent you from being active,&#x201D; says Milton. &#x201C;The bottom drawer of my filing cabinet is filled with workout clothes and sneakers.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E5. Set a timer. \u003C\u002Fb\u003E&#x201C;The longer you sit, the greater your risk of developing a cardiac disease or metabolic disease, or increasing your weight,&#x201D; says Milton. Remind yourself to get moving&#x2014;even if it&#x2019;s just for a walk to the water fountain&#x2014;with a timer from the kitchen aisle at your local grocery store. Or download free app Lark, which tracks your activities and prompts you to move with specific tips such as, &#x201C;Your seat could probably use a rest. You haven&#x2019;t moved in over an hour!&#x201D; If you have an Apple Watch, this feature is built in.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated: \u003Cb\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.glamour.com\u002Fsex-love-life\u002F2008\u002F09\u002F10-things-hes-thinking-when-youre-naked?mbid=synd_yhealth\"\u003E\u003Ci\u003E10 Things He&#x2019;s Thinking When You&#x2019;re Naked\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E6. Get handy. \u003C\u002Fb\u003EOK, this one has nothing to do with weight loss, but it&#x2019;s important for your health. If you type on a keyboard for long stretch of time, give your hands, wrists, and tendons some relief. Even if you&#x2019;re not worried about carpal tunnel syndrome right now, you can still benefit from stretches or some specialized tech. Try: Clinically Fit Inc.&#x2019;s hand exerciser ($30), a glove-like tool that will build strength and flexibility from your fingers to your elbows. Slip it on here and there to help keep your muscles loose.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E7. Tighten down below. \u003C\u002Fb\u003EWhether you&#x2019;re on the phone, in a meeting, or typing up a report, you can do kegels or butt clenches&#x2014;try holding each muscle for 15 seconds before releasing for maximum results&#x2014;with no one the wiser!\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E8. Take a (workout) break. \u003C\u002Fb\u003EThe \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002F7-min.com\u002F\"\u003Eseven minute workout\u003C\u002Fa\u003E is a super-easy online program that takes nothing more than a wall, chair and&#x2014;you guessed it!&#x2014;seven minutes of your time, making it the perfect plan to work through on your 15 minute afternoon break. Close your office door for privacy, or encourage your cubicle mates to join in. Or, \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.glamour.com\u002Fhealth-fitness\u002F2015\u002F06\u002Fthe-ultimate-10-minute-office-workout?mbid=synd_yhealth\"\u003Etry our super-fun 10-minute office workout\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, which we created with the team behind popular boutique fitness chain Physique57.\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003EBy Jillian You&#x2019;re here,&#x201D; he said.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAccording to the Anxiety and Depression Association of America, 3 to 5 percent of people suffer from depression at any given time, and the lifetime risk is 17 percent. The condition is often treated through cognitive behavioral therapy and medication. But while we don&#x2019;t know what type of treatment Padalecki has undergone, if any, outreach from fans seems to have helped on some level. He later issued the following tweet:\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" width=\"515\" height=\"219\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w515\u002Ff010a05e16529ac6f6b857a51f8b5d62cef3495e.png\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EIf Padalecki was impacted by positive affirmations, could they be helpful for other people suffering from depression? \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAbsolutely, says clinical psychologist Ben Michaelis, PhD, author of Your Next Big Thing: 10 Small Steps to Get Moving and Get Happy. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated: \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fhealth\u002Fthink-your-friend-is-depressed-heres-what-to-say-113885383892.html\"\u003E\u003Ci\u003EThink Your Friend Is Depressed? Here&#x2019;s What To Say (And What Not To)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EPositive affirmations can help people who are feeling depressed by getting them to change their focus, he tells Yahoo Health: &#x201C;When someone is depressed, nearly all of their mental energy goes toward negative thoughts and feelings. Changing the focus of one&#x2019;s thoughts can have a chain reaction from thoughts to feelings to actions.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EPositive feedback can move people with depression along in this chain and help rework the way they perceive the world and themselves, says licensed clinical psychologist Simon Rego, PsyD, director of psychology training at Montefiore Medical Center\u002FAlbert Einstein College of Medicine. Changing a person&#x2019;s thoughts can impact their feelings, he explains, so by hearing more balanced and self-affirming thoughts as well as thinking them, a person can often feel better as a result.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated: \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fhealth\u002F15-myths-and-facts-about-suicide-and-depression-94537114763.html\"\u003E\u003Ci\u003E15 Myths and Facts About Suicide and Depression\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EHow can you tell if someone is clinically depressed? Rego tells Yahoo Health that someone is typically depressed if he or she has symptoms for at least two weeks (including difficulty sleeping, appetite changes, low energy, and thoughts of life not being worth living) and these symptoms have an impact on the ability to function at home, at work, or socially.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EHave a loved one struggling with depression? In addition to encouraging them to seek treatment, Rego says there are several types of affirmations you can provide that can help: \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Col\u003E\n \u003Cli\u003EValidating statements: Trying to let the person know how hard it must be for them, and that their problems are real.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n \u003Cli\u003EAccepting statements: Letting the person know that you&#x2019;re there for them no matter what.\u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n \u003Cli\u003EEncouraging statements: Gently pushing the person to keep trying, despite how they might feel. \u003C\u002Fli\u003E\n\u003C\u002Fol\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EKindness goes a long way, too, Michaelis says: &#x201C;Just letting someone know that you care about them can have a major impact.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERead This Next: \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fhealth\u002Fwhat-facebooks-doing-to-help-prevent-suicide-112143733727.html\"\u003E\u003Ci\u003EWhat Facebook&#x2019;s Doing To Help Prevent Suicide\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003ELet&#x2019;s keep in touch! Man Who Lost His Memory at the Dentist","summary":"Root canals are routine, safe procedures right? Wrong.","body":"\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002Fc5a10913cc496e41399cd5c92ee412d6a7219102.jpg\" alt=\"The Man Who Lost His Memory at the Dentist\" width=\"540\" height=\"540\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ci\u003EEvery dentist patients horror story: leaving with \u003C\u002Fi\u003Eworse \u003Ci\u003Ehealth.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Ci\u003E(Photo: Andy Sotiriou\u002FGetty Images)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EOne morning in March of 2005, William, a British soldier stationed in Germany, woke up and headed to the dentist for a root canal. Ten years have passed, and yet upon waking every morning since that day, William still believes it&#x2019;s March of 2005, that he is a British soldier stationed in Germany, and that he will soon be headed to the dentist for a root canal. \u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated: \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fnymag.com\u002Fscienceofus\u002F2015\u002F03\u002Fstrange-case-of-the-woman-haunted-by-dragons.html?mid=yahoohealth\"\u003E\u003Ci\u003EThe Strange Case of the Woman Haunted by Dragons\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ESomething, in other words, happened between the time the surgery began and the time it ended &#x2014; something that has prevented him from forming any long-term memories since the day of his dental surgery. When he forms new memories, they now only last about 90 minutes, according to the case report his medical team recently \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov\u002Fpubmed\u002F25978125\"\u003Epublished\u003C\u002Fa\u003E in the journal \u003Ci\u003ENeurocase\u003C\u002Fi\u003E. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EThe Patient: \u003C\u002Fb\u003EWilliam was a member of the British Armed Forces, who at 22 married his wife, Samantha, \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.bbc.com\u002Ffuture\u002Fstory\u002F20150630-my-dentist-saved-my-tooth-but-stole-my-memory\"\u003Eaccording\u003C\u002Fa\u003E to the BBC, though writer David Robson notes that he changed both names to protect the couple&#x2019;s privacy. They have two children, who are now 21 and 18. On a Monday morning in March of 2005, he woke up, went to the gym, stopped in at his office to take care of some emails, and went to the dentist. &#x201C;I remember getting into the chair and the dentist inserting the local anaesthetic,&#x201D; William told Robson. It&#x2019;s the last thing he remembers. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EThe Problem\u003C\u002Fb\u003E: After the surgery, William was pale, and his eyes were &#x201C;vacant&#x201D; and unfocused, his physicians write in the case report. When he hadn&#x2019;t improved by 5 p.m., he was taken to the hospital, where he stayed for three days. There, it became clear that he&#x2019;d somehow lost his ability to form long-term memories; it was like his brain rebooted every ten minutes. While in the hospital, his memory improved a bit, so that he had a &#x201C;90-minute span of awareness,&#x201D; but it has not improved in the ten years that have passed since then. &#x201C;He wakes up believing that he should still be in the military, stationed abroad,&#x201D; the case report authors write. &#x201C;Every day he thinks it is the day of the dental appointment. \u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated: \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fnymag.com\u002Fscienceofus\u002F2015\u002F05\u002Fman-who-thought-his-family-was-evil-clones.html?mid=yahoohealth\"\u003E\u003Ci\u003EThis Man Thought His Family Was Replaced by Evil Clones\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ELike something out of \u003Ci\u003EMemento\u003C\u002Fi\u003E, his wife has entered a guide to his present life in the notes section of his smartphone, titled &#x201C;First thing &#x2014; read this.&#x201D; There, he learns every day what happened to him that day at the dentist, and that his children have now grown into young adults. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EThe Diagnosis: \u003C\u002Fb\u003EWilliam&#x2019;s symptoms would suggest that he has anterograde amnesia, an inability to create new long-term memories, while memories formed before a brain injury are accessible as normal. The cause of injury is a mystery. Imaging scans show no damage to the regions of the brain typically associated with this type of memory loss. Another possibility: Sometimes anterograde amnesia happens after psychological trauma. But William&#x2019;s wife and doctors don&#x2019;t think this quite fits his case, either, as he showed no signs of emotional problems before his memory loss.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EDr. Gerald H. Burgess, a clinical psychologist at the University of Leicester and one of the co-authors of the case report, does have a theory, outlined in the BBC write-up of the case: \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EOnce we have experienced an event, the memories are slowly cemented in the long term by altering these richly woven networks. That process of &#x201C;consolidation&#x201D; involves the production of new proteins to rebuild the synapses in their new shape; without it, the memory remains fragile and is easily eroded with time. Block that protein synthesis in rats, and they soon forget anything they have just learnt. Crucially, 90 minutes would be about the right time for this consolidation to take place &#x2013; just as William starts to forget the details of the event. Rather than losing its printing press, like Molaison, William&#x2019;s brain seems to have simply run out of ink.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003ERelated: \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fnymag.com\u002Fscienceofus\u002F2015\u002F03\u002Fwoman-whose-brain-gave-her-a-fake-accent.html?mid=yahoohealth\"\u003E\u003Ci\u003EThe Woman Whose Brain Gave Her a Fake Accent\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EBurgess hopes that after the publication of the case report, he&#x2019;ll hear from other psychiatrists and neurologists who have seen similar cases, which could eventually help William. Unless that happens, William may live the rest of his life with a memory that erases itself every 90 minutes. \u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003EBy \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fnymag.com\u002Fauthor\u002FMelissa%20Dahl\u002F\"\u003EMelissa Dahl\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EMore from \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fnymag.com\u002Fscienceofus\u002F?mid=yahoohealth\"\u003EScience of Us\u003C\u002Fa\u003E:\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fnymag.com\u002Fscienceofus\u002F2015\u002F07\u002Ftheres-a-bright-side-to-bad-dreams.html?mid=yahoohealth\"\u003EHow Your Feet Can Help You Sleep\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ca Womans Story Highlights theHidden Skin Cancer Risks for People of Color","summary":"When Jacqueline Smith discovered an almond-sized lump on her bikini line, the concerned college senior went to her campus health center to find out what it could be. She was told it was an inflamed hair follicle, but that was wrong.","body":"\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002Fb4f536060e46b7a8df3ba09dab1e2d070fb8e3be.jpg\" alt=\"One Woman&#x2019;s Story Highlights the&#xA0;Hidden Skin Cancer Risks for People of Color\" width=\"540\" height=\"394\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003E\u003Cb\u003EWhile Caucasians are more likely to be diagnosed with skin cancer, only 16 percent of cases involve advanced-stage cancer. In comparison, 52 percent of African-Americans and 26 percent of Hispanic patients are diagnosed with late-stage cases.\u003C\u002Fb\u003E (Photo: Getty Images\u002FBrand X Pictures)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EWhen Jacqueline Smith discovered an almond-sized lump on her bikini line, the concerned college senior went to her campus health center to find out what it could be. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThere, she was told not to worry &#x2014; it was simply an inflamed hair follicle. But Jacqueline couldn&#x2019;t shake the feeling that the firm, unmoving lump was something more serious. After graduation, she headed back home to Hackensack, N.J., and saw her family&#x2019;s primary care physician for a second opinion. He referred her to a surgical oncologist, who biopsied the site and had dire news: Jacqueline had skin cancer, a stage IIIC melanoma that had metastasized and was just a whisper shy of slipping into stage IV cancer. &#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EA shocking diagnosis for anyone to handle, Jacqueline was especially incredulous: She was a young African-American woman with no family history of skin cancer, and she had never engaged in behaviors like tanning that studies show correlate with a higher risk.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;I was totally shocked by the diagnosis &#x2014; my first thought was, &#x2018;Melanoma is the \u003Ci\u003Edeadly\u003C\u002Fi\u003E skin cancer&#x2019; &#x2014; I never had a reason for it to be on my radar, and never thought I had to prevent it,&#x201D; Jacqueline tells Yahoo Health. &#x201C;I had always heard melanoma was a risk for fair-skinned, middle-aged Caucasian women.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cfigure class=\"tmblr-full\"\u003E\n \u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" alt=\"image\" width=\"540\" height=\"359\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w540\u002F711e45012eb3aba60d4f9bbc1c1665fbdbfcbaca.jpg\"\u003E\n\u003C\u002Ffigure\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003E\u003Cb\u003EJacqueline Smith has survived two melanoma diagnoses. \u003C\u002Fb\u003E(Photo: Courtesy of Jacqueline Smith)\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EJacqueline, who&#x2019;s now working as the regional assistant for New York Sen. Kirsten Gillibrand, had the cancerous lymph nodes removed when she was just 21 years old. Young age and otherwise good health appeared to be on her side when subsequent scans showed no evidence of cancer, and doctors declared her clear to go on with life. Jacqueline excitedly began her first semester of a PhD program in sociology.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThen it happened again six years later, when she was 27 years old: Another lump emerged in the same area of her bikini line. Jacqueline visited the gynecologist at her university&#x2019;s health center, who said it was just an inflamed lymph node. &#x201C;If it doesn&#x2019;t bother you, don&#x2019;t bother it,&#x201D; advised the physician. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThis time, Jacqueline wasted no time in seeking a second opinion. A needle biopsy confirmed the dreaded: Stage III melanoma had returned. &#x201C;Even though it was my second diagnosis, I was shocked all over again. My doctor told me, &#x2018;It will be a miracle if you survive another five years,&#x2019;&#x201D; shares Jacqueline.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003EThe hidden skin cancer risks for people of color&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EPerhaps even more surprising is that Jacqueline&#x2019;s case isn&#x2019;t an anomaly. While Caucasians are more likely to be diagnosed with skin cancer, only 16 percent of cases involve advanced-stage cancer. In comparison, 52 percent of African-Americans and 26 percent of Hispanic patients are diagnosed with late-stage cases, according to the \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.skincancer.org\u002Fprevention\u002Fskin-cancer-and-skin-of-color\"\u003ESkin Cancer Foundation\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe initial site of Jacqueline&#x2019;s melanoma has never been determined. People of color are more likely to be diagnosed with melanoma in unusual areas like between the toes, under the nails, behind the ears, on the palms of hands and soles of feet, inside the lips, and between the buttock cheeks. Melanoma can even develop in the eyes, the lungs, the gastrointestinal tract, and the membrane known as the meninges that covers the brain and spinal cord.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ci\u003ERelated: \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fhealth\u002F3-tips-to-apply-sunscreen-the-right-way-you-know-119381099947.html\"\u003E3 Tips to Apply Sunscreen the Right Way\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;While we know UV light plays a role in melanomas found on Caucasian skin, the primary risk factors for melanoma in people with skin of color has yet to be determined,&#x201D; New York dermatologist \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.drwhitneybowe.com\"\u003EWhitney Bowe, MD\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, tells Yahoo Health. &#x201C;That&#x2019;s why patients with darker skin may get melanomas in areas that we don&#x2019;t commonly associate with sun exposure.&#x201D; \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThis time around for Jacqueline, driving the cancer back into remission was grueling. She had all of her pelvic lymph nodes removed and underwent Interferon drug treatment and radiation over the course of a year that had her coping with painful open wound burns. While she finally did achieve remission, Jacqueline was left with lymphedema in one leg, a permanent severe swelling that is caused by lymphatic system blockage.&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;I keep the lymphedema in perspective &#x2014; I have two legs that still work and I have my health, yet it&#x2019;s difficult being young and having so many restrictions. Once upon a time, just being able to choose my shoes was something I took for granted &#x2014; now, I can&#x2019;t fit into most regular shoes,&#x201D; she explains.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003ELymphedema, which Jacqueline cites as her greatest survivor challenge, is a risk associated with lymph node removal after melanoma and breast cancer surgeries. &#x201C;The risk of developing lymphedema is dependent upon the number of lymph nodes removed &#x2014; so if melanoma is diagnosed early, there may be no lymph node dissection at all, and therefore no risk of lymphedema,&#x201D; says Deborah Lindquist, MD, an oncologist with Arizona Oncology, a practice in \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.usoncology.com\"\u003Ethe US Oncology Network\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. Lindquist adds that a drug to treat the chronic condition is currently in clinical trials and may be available to the public in the near future.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EAccording to the Skin Cancer Foundation, Hispanics account for the highest amount of new skin cancer cases among people of color. &#x201C;Melanoma incidence is increasing rapidly in Latinos, who are outpacing African-Americans likely due to more tanning bed usage,&#x201D; explains New Jersey dermatologist \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fimagedermatology.com\"\u003EJeanine B. Downie\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, MD. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EExperts recommend wearing sunscreen with an SPF of 30 or higher as the best way to prevent skin cancer and melanoma in people of any color. Jacqueline now follows the advice religiously; she always has sunscreen in her bag (favorites include sprays by \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.neutrogena.com\u002Fcategory\u002Fsun\u002Fsunscreen+spray.do\"\u003ENeutrogena\u003C\u002Fa\u003E&#xA0;such as CoolDry Sport Sunscreen Spray and Ultra Sheer Body Mist Sunscreen), as she finds the spray formulas absorb without the chalkiness of other more traditional formulas. &#x201C;Please don&#x2019;t think you don&#x2019;t need sunscreen because your skin color is natural protectant from the sun &#x2014; anyone with skin is at risk for developing melanoma,&#x201D; she warns. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ci\u003ERelated: \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fhealth\u002Fthe-scary-causes-behind-the-rise-in-skin-cancer-118288125190.html\"\u003EThe Scary Causes Behind the Rise in Skin Cancer Rates\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EMost importantly, experts say to get familiar with your skin, so that you notice any changes to new or existing spots and moles. Melanoma is virtually always curable if detected early. &#x201C;If the mole is multicolored, very dark, growing rapidly in size, painful, or stands out as totally different from your other moles, have a dermatologist check it out,&#x201D; Downie says. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EHave an annual skin checkup with your dermatologist to assess new and old spots, and if you&#x2019;ve previously had precancerous or cancerous lesions, you should go even more regularly &#x2014; every six months. When visiting other doctors like your ophthalmologist and gynecologist, have them check for any unusual signs that you can&#x2019;t see, and ask the same of your hair stylist, who experts say is often your first line of defense against skin cancer on the scalp. &#xA0; &#xA0;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EIn fact, New York hair stylist Roman Kusayev of the \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fromanksalon.com\"\u003ERoman K Salon\u003C\u002Fa\u003E recently detected a melanoma on a regular Latina client&#x2019;s scalp while applying hair color. &#x201C;I noticed a suspicious slightly red spot on her scalp that clearly wasn&#x2019;t a wound or scab. I didn&#x2019;t want to scare her, but I knew I had the responsibility to bring it to her attention,&#x201D; Kusayev tells Yahoo Health. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EThe client soon made an appointment with her dermatologist, who diagnosed the lesion as skin cancer. Fortunately, the early detection made for routine removal. Hairstyles like tightly parted ponytails and tight braids can leave the scalp vulnerable to the sun&#x2019;s UV rays. Experts recommend wearing a hat or brushing hair back when out in the sun so as not to harshly part and expose swaths of scalp to UV rays. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003EIf you do see something pop up that gives you a funny feeling, Jacqueline says to always trust your instinct. &#x201C;It&#x2019;s important to be your own health advocate. I didn&#x2019;t stop harassing doctors until I definitively found out what was wrong, and that is what saved my life.&#x201D; \u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E\u003Ci\u003ERead This Next: \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Fhealth\u002Fthe-part-of-your-face-you-absolutely-need-to-122973275813.html\"\u003EThe Part of Your Face You Absolutely Need to Protect From the Sun \u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fi\u003E\u003C\u002Fb\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ci\u003ELet&#x2019;s keep in touch!
